# Excel Vba Managing Files And Data

> In this course, Curt Frye—president of Technology and Society, Incorporated—guides you through effective ways to simplify your management of files and data with Excel VBA, a robust and flexible programming environment for Microsoft Excel workbooks. Using VBA to automate repetitive data import and management tasks can save you substantial time and streamline your processes. Learn how to create a fi

#### Select the active region
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One very common action in Microsoft Excel that you don't always think about is selecting the current region or the active region.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=9)** And in this movie, I will show you how to do that in the worksheet and also using Excel VBA.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=15)** My sample file is 0 1 0 1 CurrentRegion and you can find it in the Chapter01 folder of the exercise files collection.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=24)** In this workbook I have a single worksheet and in it I have sales data by Year and also by State.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=31)** The active cell is currently B7, but it could be any cell in this range.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=37)** For example, I just changed to C3.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=40)** And the active region is every cell that is near the current cell that is the active cell and contains data and it is represented as a rectangle.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=52)** You can see it most clearly if you create a table based on the data list that I have.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=58)** So, on the home tab of the ribbon, and, again, making sure that one of the cells in the data list is the active cell, I will click the Format as Table button and then select a table style, just do the one at the top left, and Excel has identified the current region or the active region.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=79)** And you can see it indicated here with what's called a marquee or border.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=85)** And then in the Create Table dialogue box, you have the range of A1 through C15.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=92)** And, in fact, that is the range that contains the data in the current region.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=98)** So, that's what it looks like when Excel does it as part of creating a table, I'll click Cancel.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=104)** If you want to select the active region using the keyboard, you can press CTRL + Shift + 8.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=112)** So, you're typing basically Control and then asterisk.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=116)** So I'll do that now, CTRL + Shift + 8, and I have selected the active region.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=123)** If you want to do the same thing using Excel VBA, then you just need to use one fairly straightforward command.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=132)** I've selected a cell inside of the range.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=135)** And then I'll press Alt + F11 to move to the Visual Basic Editor.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=139)** And rather than make you type all of the code, I have started with my subroutine's name and then also defined a variable as a string.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/select-the-active-region?u=76281980&t=150)** And I've left space for a command.
>

> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=159)** If I had XL And, then it would need to be both.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=162)** And of course we can't have two values in the same cell, so we would get nothing back.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=168)** However, with Or, we can have multiple values.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=172)** So I'll click inside of the subroutine and then press F5 to run it.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=177)** Then Alt F11 to go back and I see the results for California and Arizona and the year is 2023 and 2024.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=189)** Also at the top I have the filter for state, and the filter arrow indicates that there is an active filter.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=198)** And if you hover the mouse pointer over it, it shows you what that filter is.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=204)** I'll leave the worksheet in its current state and then press Alt F11 to move back to the visual basic editor.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=210)** And I will resize my code window so that you can see the next item, which is called multiple items.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=218)** Everything is the same, string address, selection, auto filter, and then finding the string address, until we get down to this last line.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=228)** We start out with the auto filter and it's still operating on field two.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=234)** However, the criteria, specifically criteria number one, is an array of values, and those are listed here.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=242)** We have Arizona, California, and Oregon.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=245)** And those are in double quotes because they are strings.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=249)** Then after comma, we have our operator XL filter values.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=253)** That keyword is used when you have an array of values, any one of which can be matched.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=261)** You might wonder why we have criteria one and criteria two at the start, and then we have an array for more than two values.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=269)** And the reason is that in Excel VBA, in the early days, you could only have two filter values on a single column.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=282)** So for a field you could have one value shown, or two, but no more.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=287)** It wasn't until Excel VBA, in fact, Excel had been around for a number of years that you could add three or more values to your filter.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=296)** So that's why you have the two different ways of calculating or creating and defining Excel filters.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=304)** And of course, they kept the original way of doing it with two criteria and XL Or for backwards compatibility so that old worksheets could continue to work.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=314)** But the new way of coding it is here in multiple items.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=319)** So let's see how that works.
>
> **[5:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=321)** I've clicked inside of the multiple items, subroutine.
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=324)** I'll press F5. My code's been run, ALT F11.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/combine-criteria-using-or?u=76281980&t=328)** And there I have the results for Oregon, California, and Arizona for the years of 2023 and 2024.

> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=241)** And this is where the On Error Resume Next and On Error GoTo 0 lines of code come into play.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=249)** On Error Resume Next is an error handling mode, where Microsoft Excel, specifically the Visual Basic Editor, tries to keep running the code for as long as it can.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=259)** It basically ignores all errors and keeps executing.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=263)** And that's fine, but there will be times when the program will stop running anyway because the Visual Basic Editor just can't figure out what to do next because of variables that are missing or something.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=276)** However, if you do it under specific controlled circumstances, it can help you get through the code effectively.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=284)** And here what we're doing is avoiding the error we just saw when we try to close a file that is not open.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=290)** The irregular error handling mode, which we saw earlier, is created by On Error GoTo 0.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=296)** So basically we're turning error handling off, attempting to close a workbook, ignoring any errors if they occur, and then going back to our regular error handling.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=306)** So now, Target.xlxs is still closed.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=308)** I'll press F5 to run.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=311)** And it appears that nothing happened.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=313)** But in fact, what's happening is that Excel is trying to run the code, but instead of showing an error because we turned error handling off, it just goes on to the next line.
>
> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/close-a-workbook?u=76281980&t=326)** So those are the ways that you can close workbooks and also avoid errors if you try to close a workbook that is already closed.

> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=156)** The space and underscore indicates to the Visual Basic Editor that I'm continuing the same line of code just on a different line within the module.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=165)** So then I'll press Return and then Tab so that I have some white space, and the indentation indicates that I'm continuing the previous line of code.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=176)** I also need to specify the file format, so that would be FileFormat :=.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=183)** And then we'll use a built-in Excel variable, and that is xlCSV.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=190)** So we have our file name with the .csv extension, and then the file format using the built-in variable xlCSV.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=200)** Right, everything looks good, so I'll click down below and press F5 to run.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=205)** And the file has been saved.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=207)** And if you note up at the top, then we have SaveAsCSV.csv as the active file name.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=215)** So we are no longer working in the previous edition, we are working in this one.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=220)** Now let's see what happens if I try to save this file as SaveAsCSV.csv again.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=227)** So I'll press F5, and we get an alert box asking if we want to overwrite it.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=232)** I'll click Cancel, and I have a failure error, so I'll click End rather than going into debugging mode.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=241)** And this is where the Application.DisplayAlerts lines come in handy.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=247)** So I will remove the single quote so they are no longer comments, they're actual code that will run.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=253)** And what Application.DisplayAlerts = False will do is prevent the alert box that we just saw from appearing.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=260)** So even if the file already exists, it will be overwritten.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=264)** So I'll press F5 to run, and the code ran as expected.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=269)** One last thing to note is that the CSV file that we created does not contain macros or any of our table formatting.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=279)** So if I close the Visual Basic editor and then close the file here, and I won't save my changes, and then open the CSV version of the file in the Exercise Files folder, you'll see here that I just have the data with no table formatting.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=300)** And if I press Alt + F11, there is nothing in the Visual Basic Editor as well.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=306)** So one of the strengths of the CSV file format is that you have your data and it is very portable.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/save-a-workbook-as-a-csv-file?u=76281980&t=314)** The problem is that you lose a lot of built-in Excel capabilities.

#### Move a worksheet to an existing workbook
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/move-a-worksheet-to-an-existing-workbook?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/move-a-worksheet-to-an-existing-workbook?u=76281980&t=0)** - One of the great things about Excel is that you can use workbooks to store collections of data.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/move-a-worksheet-to-an-existing-workbook?u=76281980&t=5)** And because worksheets tend to store data that is saved based on a theme, you can create workbooks to save them as you move along.
>

> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=256)** The year will always be four days, at least for a long time to come.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=259)** The month will now always be two digits, and the same thing for the day.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=264)** So then, here, I have CreateWithDate, a subroutine that will create a worksheet that will have the name of the date string we just created.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=277)** And note that we don't have to pass any value to the CreateDateString function because we're using the system, and built-in keywords such as year, month, and day, to get the values we need.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=290)** And I will note that I'm not doing any error checking here, because I wanted to keep the code simple.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=296)** Doing error checking is one of the elementary VBA skills that I assume that you have when you took the course.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=304)** So from here I can run the code for F5, and I get my new worksheet.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=309)** So I'll press ALT + F11, and at the bottom I have a sheet called 20250119.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=316)** And it's important to remember that the order will always be year, two-digit month, and then two-digit day.
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=324)** And this makes this particular rendition of the date easier to sort.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=329)** It will always sort by the year, then by the month, and then by the day.
>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=334)** If you were to put the day first, then you would have the 19th of February before the 20th of January, because it would go 1902 instead of 2001.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=346)** The order should be the other way.
>
> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/use-the-current-date-and-time?u=76281980&t=348)** So, I find year, month, day, to be much easier to work with.

> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=185)** And this indicates to the Visual Basic editor that I want to continue the same line of code even though they're on two different physical lines within the code module.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=196)** Now I need to identify the source data.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=198)** So we have SourceData and it's a parameter, so colon equal, and then in quotes, B2:B8.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=207)** And because we are on the ActiveSheet, I don't need to identify anything further, right?
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=215)** Everything looks good. So I'll press F5 to run.

>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=228)** There are seven spaces.

>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=236)** We don't know how much, but we do know that we did better than the target.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=240)** Reds indicate that we are below our target and the blank here for Thursday shows that we tied our goal.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=249)** So we hit it exactly.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=250)** It's neither a win or a loss.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/create-a-win-loss-sparkline?u=76281980&t=253)** So if you're looking for whether specific goals were met or not or tied, then a win loss sparkline is a great way to go.

>
> **[6:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/add-an-option-button-to-a-userform?u=76281980&t=406)** So Ground and Overnight can't be selected at the same time, but as you see here, Signature and Insurance can be, and that is how you include option buttons and check boxes in a user form.

### 7. Managing PivotTables Using VBA

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### Record a PivotTable configuration
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] When you work with pivot tables, you'll often find that you want to recreate a particular configuration.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=7)** You could write down the fields and the order in which they appear, but it is far easier to record a macro that configures the pivot table for you, and in this movie, I will show you how to do that, and then we'll look at the code.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=19)** My sample file is 07_01_RecordPosition, and you can find it in the Chapter 7 folder of the Exercise Files collection.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=28)** In this workbook, I already have a worksheet named Pivot, which has a pivot table on it, and it is based on the data found on Sheet 1.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=39)** My goal is to record a macro that will change the position of the pivot table to a different configuration.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=51)** Code to work with a pivot table is very involved, so it works best if you record what you want to do.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=59)** Also, because you're recording every step that you take, you want to rehearse a few times, and even write down a script so you can follow it.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=67)** With all that in mind, let's record a macro.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=70)** So I'll go to the View tab of the ribbon, and then on the right side, there is the Macros button.

>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=82)** In the Record Macro dialogue box, I will give the macro a name of RecordPosition.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=89)** I won't worry about anything else.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=92)** So to start recording, I'll click Okay, and Excel is now recording everything that I do.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=99)** My first step will be to click a cell inside of the pivot table.

> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=103)** So I'll click there, and then I'll go to the Pivot Table Analyze contextual tab of the ribbon.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=110)** In the Actions group, I'll click the Clear button, and then click Clear All.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=116)** So the pivot table remains, but all of the fields and other settings have been erased.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=122)** It's important to clear the configuration of your pivot table as the first thing you do, because otherwise the code might try to refer to an element of the pivot table that is not present, for example, a field that was there when recorded might not be there when you try to run the macro.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=139)** So it is always best when working with a pivot table to clear the existing pivot table and build up from the bottom.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/record-a-pivottable-configuration?u=76281980&t=148)** So with all that in mind, let's create our pivot table configuration.
>

> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/copy-data-from-a-list-using-take?u=76281980&t=270)** Now click in cell G4, and we'll create another TAKE function.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/copy-data-from-a-list-using-take?u=76281980&t=275)** So that will be TAKE.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/copy-data-from-a-list-using-take?u=76281980&t=277)** The array is A4:B10.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/copy-data-from-a-list-using-take?u=76281980&t=281)** Again, we want to return both columns of data, and then a comma.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/copy-data-from-a-list-using-take?u=76281980&t=285)** The number of rows is not 6 because that would come from the top of the list.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/copy-data-from-a-list-using-take?u=76281980&t=291)** Instead, we want -6, so I'll type a minus sign, and then H1, comma, and two columns worth of data, which is all that we have.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/copy-data-from-a-list-using-take?u=76281980&t=300)** Then right parenthesis and Enter, and we get our values.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/copy-data-from-a-list-using-take?u=76281980&t=305)** So everything from 2019 through to the end of 2024.
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/copy-data-from-a-list-using-take?u=76281980&t=312)** If we were asked for only values from 2021 and later, then I could go up to E1, 2021, Enter, and the formula updates so we only see those four years worth of data.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/copy-data-from-a-list-using-take?u=76281980&t=328)** And, of course, if I wanted to return values from the top of the list, then rather than using -H1, so we have -4, I would instead use the value in H1 and we would get the first four rows just as we did here.

> [!info]- Semantic Content

#### Delete data from a list using DROP
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In the previous movie, I showed you how to use the TAKE function to bring row from a dataset to a different part of your worksheet.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=10)** In this movie, I will show you how to perform similar actions using the DROP function, which is similar but has some distinct differences.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=21)** My sample file is 08_05_Drop, and you can find it in the Chapter08 folder of the Exercise Files collection.

> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=66)** So in D4, I'll type =DROP drop the array, again A4 through B10, we're not including the headers, then a comma, and then the number of rows.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=77)** The Excel team assumed that you'll want to drop the oldest values, which tend to be at the top of a list.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=84)** So positive values indicate the number of rows from the top to drop, and that is the opposite of TAKE, where you would use a positive number to take values from the bottom.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=97)** So we have two, and then we don't want to exclude any columns.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=101)** So rather than like with the TAKE function where we would say, "I want to take two columns of data," here, we would need to say how many to exclude.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=113)** We don't want to exclude either, so I will leave it blank.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=117)** Right parentheses and Enter.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/delete-data-from-a-list-using-drop?u=76281980&t=120)** And we get all of our data except for the two oldest rows, so 2018 and 2019 have been dropped.
>

>

>

>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/further-resources?u=76281980&t=12)** The first is "Excel 2019 Power Programming with VBA" by Michael Alexander and Dick Kusleika.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/further-resources?u=76281980&t=19)** It's an excellent book, and even though it was written for Excel 2019, there is a lot that you can still use in your current version of Excel.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/further-resources?u=76281980&t=28)** So the fact that it's an older book should not put you off.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/further-resources?u=76281980&t=32)** Second is "Microsoft Excel VBA and Macros," specifically written for Office 2021 and Microsoft 365.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/further-resources?u=76281980&t=40)** That's by Bill Jelen and Tracy Syrstad.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/further-resources?u=76281980&t=44)** That's another great book, and even though it's a few years old, everything in it still applies.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/further-resources?u=76281980&t=51)** And finally, the oldest book of all, but by far the most complete, is "Professional Excel Development, Second Edition" by Rob Bovey, Dennis Wallentin, Stephen Bullen and John Green.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/further-resources?u=76281980&t=62)** This is an outstanding book, and if you are serious about Excel programming, not just doing it every now and then, but really getting good at it, I cannot recommend "Professional Excel Development" enough.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-vba-managing-files-and-data-25320834/further-resources?u=76281980&t=75)** With these three books on your shelf and what you learned in this course, there will be nothing that you won't be able to do with Excel VBA.
